#STUDY
ST:STUDY_TITLE                   	Serum lipids are associated with nonalcoholic fatty liver disease: a pilot
ST:STUDY_TITLE                   	case-control study in Mexico
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	A nested case-control study was conducted with a sample of 98 NAFLD cases and
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	100 healthy controls who are participating in an on-going, longitudinal study in
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	Mexico. NAFLD cases were clinically confirmed using elevated liver enzyme tests
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	and liver ultrasound or liver ultrasound elastography, after excluding alcohol
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	abuse, and 100 controls were identified as having at least two consecutive
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	normal alanine aminotransferase (ALT) and aspartate aminotransferase (AST)
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	(&lt; 40 U/L) results in a 6-month period, and a normal liver ultrasound
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	elastography result in January 2018. Samples were analyzed on the Sciex
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	Lipidyzer Platform and quantified with normalization to serum volume. As many as
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	1100 lipid species can be identified using the Lipidyzer targeted
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	multiple-reaction monitoring list. The association between serum lipids and
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	NAFLD was investigated using analysis of covariance, random forest analysis, and
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	by generating receiver operator characteristic (ROC) curves.
ST:INSTITUTE                     	University of California, Los Angeles
ST:DEPARTMENT                    	Biological Chemistry
ST:LABORATORY                    	UCLA Lipidomics
ST:LAST_NAME                     	Williams
ST:FIRST_NAME                    	Kevin
ST:ADDRESS                       	BSRB 257, 615 Charles E. Young Drive S., Los Angeles, CA, 90095
ST:EMAIL                         	lipidomics@mednet.ucla.edu
ST:PHONE                         	3108254397
ST:SUBMIT_DATE                   	2022-02-09

#COLLECTION
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	A convenience sample of 98 NAFLD cases and 100 healthy controls aged 36 to
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	78 years, who are long-term participants in the HWCS was used for the current
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	pilot study. The inclusion criteria for this study were having a
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	hepatologist-confirmed diagnosis of NAFLD for the cases, and a history of normal
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	ALT and AST results (&lt; 40 U/L) plus a normal ultrasound elastography
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	result for the controls. Liver enzymes (ALT, AST), total cholesterol,
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	high-density lipoprotein (HDL-C), low-density lipoprotein cholesterol (LDL-C),
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	triglycerides, glucose, body mass index (BMI), waist circumference, and blood
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	pressure were measured. Participants reported fasting for ≥12 h at blood
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	draw. Serum samples that were collected during 2011–2013 and stored at
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	− 70 °C, as well as self-reported data and laboratory results that were
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	obtained during the same time period, were used for the cases and controls.
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/34629052/
CO:SAMPLE_TYPE                   	Blood (serum)
#TREATMENT

#SAMPLEPREP
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Bligh and Dyer lipid extraction for subsequent lipidomics analysis using the
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Sciex Lipidyzer Mass Spectrometry Platform (Bligh and Dyer, 1959). The protocol
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	is a modified version of the Serum Extraction Protocol published in the
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Lipidyzer Platform user guide (Sciex, 2016). For internal standard preparation,
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	see Chemical preparations of the Lipidyzer Platform user guide (Sciex, 2016) and
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	(Ubhi, 2018). For more details, check the following published protocol:
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC7753944/

#MS
MS:INSTRUMENT_NAME               	ABI Sciex 5500 QTrap
MS:INSTRUMENT_TYPE               	QTRAP
MS:MS_TYPE                       	Other
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	Hardware/System Setup: The Lipidyzer platform hardware has been described
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	previously. (10) The Turbo V source is outfitted with a 65 μm ESI Electrode and
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	the transfer line is plumbed with 50 μm ID PEEKsil tubing from the Lipidyzer
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	installation kit. For the SLA application method, a 100 μL loop was installed.
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	SLA Overview: The Shotgun Lipidomics Assistant (SLA) oversees three processes in
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	the DMS lipidomics workflow: (1) analyzing DMS tuning data to update methods
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	utilizing the DMS, (2) analyzing QC/suitability test data to measure relative
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	lipid standard response, and (3) analyzing DMS lipidomics data files to yield
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	processed quantitative results. This third process is subdivided into three
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	parts: (1) extracting data from Analyst data files, (2) merging extracted data
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	with the sample map and performing normalization, and (3) creating plots and
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	data sheets of the class total and triacylglycerol data. These five processes
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	are carried out on separate tabs within the SLA GUI. We will describe each of
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	these five processes and the computations performed in detail below. While the
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	LWM scripted the creation of Analyst sample batches and performed data analysis
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	for these three processes, our workflow allows the user to setup the batches
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	manually in Analyst and performs the analysis on the resulting data. This manual
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	batch creation step requires a minimal amount of user time and gives the user
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	flexibility in performing tuning, QC/suitability tests, and analyzing
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	experimental data. The first step of analysis within each of the three primary
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	processes is the conversion of the WIFF files to mzML format using
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	Proteowizard’s MSconvertGUI application. (11) The SLA reads the resulting mzML
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	files utilizing the pyOpenMS package (12) and converts the data into readable
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	data tables for further data processing. Please refer to the following
MS:MS_COMMENTS                   	publication for more details: https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/34637296/
MS:ION_MODE                      	POSITIVE
